<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89M6"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89M7">“They’re Slow Mutants,” the gunslinger said. “I don’t think they’ll bother us. They’re probably just as frightened of us as we are of—”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89M8"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89M9">One of the forms broke free and shambled toward them. The face was that of a starving idiot. The faint naked body had been transformed into a knotted mess of tentacular limbs and suckers.</span></p>
<a aid="F89MA"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89MB"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89MC">The boy screamed again and crowded against the gunslinger’s leg like a frightened dog.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89MD"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89ME">One of the thing’s tentacle arms pawed across the flat platform of the handcar. It reeked of the wet and the dark. The gunslinger let loose of the handle and drew. He put a bullet through the forehead of the starving idiot face. It fell away, its faint swamp-fire glow fading, an eclipsed moon. The gunflash lay bright and branded on their dark retinas, fading only reluctantly. The smell of expended powder was hot and savage and alien in this buried place.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89MF"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89MG">There were others, more of them. None moved against them overtly, but they were closing in on the tracks, a silent, hideous party of rubberneckers.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89MH"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89MI">“You may have to pump for me,” the gunslinger said. “Can you?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89MJ"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89MK">“Yes.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89ML"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89MM">“Then be ready.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89MN"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89MO">The boy stood close to him, his body poised. His eyes took in the Slow Mutants only as they passed, not traversing, not seeing more than they had to. The boy assumed a psychic bulge of terror, as if his very id had somehow sprung out through his pores to form a shield. If he had the touch, the gunslinger reasoned, that was not impossible.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89MP"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89MQ">The gunslinger pumped steadily but did not increase his speed. The Slow Mutants could smell their terror, he knew that, but he doubted if terror alone would be enough to motivate them. He and the boy were, after all, creatures of the light, and whole. <span class="italic" aid="F89MR">How they must hate us,</span> he thought, and wondered if they had hated the man in black in the same way. He thought not, or perhaps he had passed among them only like the shadow of a dark wing in this greater darkness.</span></p>
<a aid="F89MS"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89MT"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89MU">The boy made a noise in his throat and the gunslinger turned his head almost casually. Four of them were charging the handcar in a stumbling way—one of them in the process of finding a handgrip.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89MV"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89N0">The gunslinger let go of the handle and drew again, with the same sleepy casual motion. He shot the lead mutant in the head. The mutant made a sighing, sobbing noise and began to grin. Its hands were limp and fish-like, dead; the fingers clove to one another like the fingers of a glove long immersed in drying mud. One of these corpse-hands found the boy’s foot and began to pull.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89N1"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89N2">The boy shrieked aloud in the granite womb.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89N3"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89N4">The gunslinger shot the mutant in the chest. It began to slobber through the grin. Jake was going off the side. The gunslinger caught one of his arms and was almost pulled off balance himself. The thing was surprisingly strong. The gunslinger put another bullet in the mutant’s head. One eye went out like a candle. Still it pulled. They engaged in a silent tug of war for Jake’s jerking, wriggling body. The Slow Mutants yanked on him like a wishbone. The wish would undoubtedly be to dine.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89N5"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89N6">The handcar was slowing down. The others began to close in—the lame, the halt, the blind. Perhaps they only looked for a Jesus to heal them, to raise them Lazarus-like from the darkness.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89N7"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89N8"><span class="italic" aid="F89N9">It’s the end for the boy,</span> the gunslinger thought with perfect coldness. <span class="italic" aid="F89NA">This is the end he meant. Let go and pump or hold on and be buried. The end for the boy.</span></span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89NB"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89NC">He gave a tremendous yank on the boy’s arm and shot the mutant in the belly. For one frozen moment its grip grew even tighter and Jake began to slide off the edge again. Then the dead mud-mitts loosened, and the Slow Mutie fell on its face behind the slowing handcar, still grinning.</span></p>
<a aid="F89ND"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89NE"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89NF">“I thought you’d leave me,” the boy was sobbing. “I thought . . . I thought . . .”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89NG"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89NH">“Hold on to my belt,” the gunslinger said. “Hold on just as tight as you can.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89NI"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89NJ">The hand worked into his belt and clutched there; the boy was breathing in great convulsive, silent gasps.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89NK"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89NL">The gunslinger began to pump steadily again, and the handcar picked up speed. The Slow Mutants fell back a step and watched them go with faces hardly human (or pathetically so), faces that generated the weak phosphorescence common to those weird deep-sea fishes that live under incredible black pressure, faces that held no anger or hate but only what seemed to be a semiconscious, idiot regret.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89NM"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89NN">“They’re thinning,” the gunslinger said. The drawn-up muscles of his lower belly and privates relaxed the smallest bit. “They’re—”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89NO"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89NP">The Slow Mutants had put rocks across the track. The way was blocked. It had been a quick, poor job, perhaps the work of only a minute to clear, but they were stopped. And someone would have to get down and move them. The boy moaned and shuddered closer to the gunslinger. The gunslinger let go of the handle and the handcar coasted noiselessly to the rocks, where it thumped to rest.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89NQ"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89NR">The Slow Mutants began to close in again, almost casually, almost as if they had been passing by, lost in a dream of darkness, and had found someone of whom to ask directions. A street-corner congregation of the damned beneath the ancient rock.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89NS"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89NT">“Are they going to get us?” the boy asked calmly.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89NU"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89NV">“Never in life. Be quiet a second.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89O0"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89O1">He looked at the rocks. The mutants were weak, of course, and had not been able to drag any of the boulders to block <a aid="F89O2"></a>their way. Only small rocks. Only enough to stop them, to make someone—</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89O3"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89O4">“Get down,” the gunslinger said. “You’ll have to move them. I’ll cover you.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89O5"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89O6">“No,” the boy whispered. “Please.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89O7"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89O8">“I can’t give you a gun and I can’t move the rocks and shoot, too. You have to get down.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89O9"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89OA">Jake’s eyes rolled terribly; for a moment his body shuddered in tune with the turnings of his mind, and then he wriggled over the side and began to throw rocks to the right and the left, working with mad speed, not looking up.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89OB"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89OC">The gunslinger drew and waited.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89OD"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89OE">Two of them, lurching rather than walking, went for the boy with arms like dough. The guns did their work, stitching the darkness with red-white lances of light that pushed needles of pain into the gunslinger’s eyes. The boy screamed and continued to throw away rocks to either side. Witch-glow leaped and danced. Hard to see now, that was the worst. Everything had gone to shadows and afterimages.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89OF"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89OG">One of them, glowing hardly at all, suddenly reached for the boy with rubber boogeyman arms. Eyes that ate up half the mutie’s head rolled wetly.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89OH"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89OI">Jake screamed again and turned to struggle.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89OJ"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89OK">The gunslinger fired without allowing himself to think before his spotty vision could betray his hands into a terrible quiver; the two heads were only inches apart. It was the mutie who fell.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89OL"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89OM">Jake threw rocks wildly. The mutants milled just outside the invisible line of trespass, closing a little at a time, now very close. Others had caught up, swelling their number.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89ON"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89OO">“All right,” the gunslinger said. “Get on. Quick.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89OP"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89OQ">When the boy moved, the mutants came at them. Jake was <a aid="F89OR"></a>over the side and scrambling to his feet; the gunslinger was already pumping again, all out. Both guns were holstered now. They must run. It was their only chance.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89OS"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89OT">Strange hands slapped the metal plane of the car’s surface. The boy was holding his belt with both hands now, his face pressed tightly into the small of the gunslinger’s back.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89OU"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89OV">A group of them ran onto the tracks, their faces full of that mindless, casual anticipation. The gunslinger was full of adrenaline; the car was flying along the tracks into the darkness. They struck the four or five pitiful hulks full force. They flew like rotten bananas struck from the stem.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89P0"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89P1">On and on, into the soundless, flying, banshee darkness.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89P2"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89P3">After an age, the boy raised his face into the made wind, dreading and yet needing to know. The ghost of gunflashes still lingered on his retinas. There was nothing to see but the darkness and nothing to hear but the rumble of the river.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89P4"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89P5">“They’re gone,” the boy said, suddenly fearing an end to the tracks in the darkness, and the wounding crash as they jumped the rails and plunged to twisted ruin. He had ridden in cars; once his humorless father had driven at ninety on the New Jersey Turnpike and had been stopped by a cop who ignored the twenty Elmer Chambers offered with his license and gave him a ticket anyway. But he had never ridden like this, with the wind and the blindness and the terrors behind and ahead, with the sound of the river like a chuckling voice—the voice of the man in black. The gunslinger’s arms were pistons in a lunatic human factory.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89P6"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89P7">“They’re gone,” the boy said timidly, the words ripped from his mouth by the wind. “You can slow down now. We left them behind.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89P8"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89P9">But the gunslinger did not hear. They careened onward into the strange dark.</span></p>
<a aid="F89PA"></a>
<div class="calibre_5" aid="F89PB"> </div><h3 class="calibre_8" aid="F89PC"><span class="calibre9" aid="F89PD"><span class="bold1" aid="F89PE">XI</span></span></h3><div class="calibre_1" aid="F89PF"> </div>
<p class="calibre_13" aid="F89PG"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89PH">They went on for three “days” without incident.</span></p>
<div class="calibre_5" aid="F89PI"> </div><h3 class="calibre_8" aid="F89PJ"><span class="calibre9" aid="F89PK"><span class="bold1" aid="F89PL">XII</span></span></h3><div class="calibre_1" aid="F89PM"> </div>
<p class="calibre_9" aid="F89PN"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89PO">During the fourth period of waking (halfway through? three-quarters? they didn’t know—knew only that they weren’t tired enough yet to stop) there was a sharp thump beneath them; the handcar swayed, and their bodies immediately leaned to the right against gravity as the rails took a gradual turn to the left.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89PP"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89PQ">There was a light ahead—a glow so faint and alien that it seemed at first to be a totally new element, not earth, air, fire, nor water. It had no color and could only be discerned by the fact that they had regained their hands and faces in a dimension beyond that of touch. Their eyes had become so light-sensitive that they noticed the glow more than five miles before they approached its source.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89PR"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89PS">“The end,” the boy said tightly. “It’s the end.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89PT"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89PU">“No.” The gunslinger spoke with odd assurance. “It isn’t.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89PV"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89Q0">And it was not. They reached light but not day.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89Q1"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89Q2">As they approached the source of the glow, they saw for the first time that the rock wall to the left had fallen away and their tracks had been joined by others which crossed in a complex spiderweb. The light laid them in burnished vectors. On some of them there were dark boxcars, passenger coaches, a stage that had been adapted to rails. They made the gunslinger nervous, like ghost galleons trapped in an underground Sargasso.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89Q3"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89Q4">The light grew stronger, hurting their eyes a little, but growing slowly enough to allow them to adapt. They came from dark to light like divers coming up from deep fathoms in slow stages.</span></p>
<a aid="F89Q5"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89Q6"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89Q7">Ahead, drawing nearer, was a huge hangar stretching up into the dark. Cut into it, showing yellow squares of light, were a series of perhaps twenty-four entranceways, growing from the size of toy windows to a height of twenty feet as they drew closer. They passed inside through one of the middle ways. Written above were a series of characters, in various languages, the gunslinger presumed. He was astounded to find that he could read the last one; it was an ancient root of the High Speech itself and said:</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89Q8"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89Q9">TRACK 10 TO SURFACE AND POINTS WEST</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89QA"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89QB">The light inside was brighter; the tracks met and merged through a series of switchings. Here some of the traffic lanterns still worked, flashing eternal reds and greens and ambers.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89QC"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89QD">They rolled between the rising stone piers caked black with the passage of thousands of vehicles, and then they were in some kind of central terminal. The gunslinger let the handcar coast slowly to a stop, and they peered around.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89QE"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89QF">“It’s like a subway,” the boy said.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89QG"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89QH">“Subway?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89QI"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89QJ">“Never mind. You wouldn’t know what I was talking about. <span class="italic" aid="F89QK">I</span> don’t even know what I’m talking about, not anymore.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89QL"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89QM">The boy climbed up onto the cracked cement. They looked at silent, deserted booths where newspapers and books had once been traded or sold; a bootery; a weapon shop (the gunslinger, suddenly feverish with excitement, saw revolvers and rifles; closer inspection showed that their barrels had been filled with lead; he did, however, pick out a bow, which he slung over his back, and a quiver of almost useless, badly weighted arrows); a women’s apparel shop. Somewhere a converter was turning the air over and over, as it had for thousands of years—but perhaps would not for much longer. It had a grating noise somewhere in its cycle which served to remind that perpetual motion, even under strictly controlled conditions, was still a fool’s dream. The air had a <a aid="F89QN"></a>mechanized taste. The boy’s shoes and the gunslinger’s boots made flat echoes.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89QO"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89QP">The boy cried out: “Hey! Hey . . .”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89QQ"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89QR">The gunslinger turned around and went to him. The boy was standing, transfixed, at the book stall. Inside, sprawled in the far corner, was a mummy. It was wearing a blue uniform with gold piping—a trainman’s uniform, by the look. There was an ancient, perfectly preserved newspaper on the dead thing’s lap, and it crumbled to dust when the gunslinger touched it. The mummy’s face was like an old, shriveled apple. Cautiously, the gunslinger touched the cheek. There was a small puff of dust. When it cleared, they were able to look through the flesh and into the mummy’s mouth. A gold tooth twinkled there.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89QS"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89QT">“Gas,” the gunslinger murmured. “The old people made a gas that would do this. Or so Vannay told us.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89QU"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89QV">“The one who taught from books.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89R0"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89R1">“Yes. He.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89R2"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89R3">“I bet these old people fought wars with it,” the boy said darkly. “Killed <span class="italic" aid="F89R4">other</span> old people with it.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89R5"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89R6">“I’m sure you’re right.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89R7"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89R8">There were perhaps a dozen other mummies. All but two or three were wearing the blue and gold ornamental uniforms. The gunslinger supposed that the gas had been used when the place was empty of most incoming and outgoing traffic. Perhaps once in the dim ago, the station had been a military objective of some long-gone army and cause.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89R9"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89RA">The thought depressed him.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89RB"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89RC">“We better go on,” he said, and started toward Track 10 and the handcar again. But the boy stood rebelliously behind him.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89RD"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89RE">“Not going.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89RF"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89RG">The gunslinger turned back, surprised.</span></p>
<a aid="F89RH"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89RI"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89RJ">The boy’s face was twisted and trembling. “You won’t get what you want until I’m dead. I’ll take my chances by myself.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89RK"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89RL">The gunslinger nodded noncommittally, hating himself for what he was going to do. “Okay, Jake,” he said mildly. “Long days, pleasant nights.” He turned around, walked across to the stone piers, leaped easily down onto the handcar.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89RM"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89RN">“You made a deal with someone!” the boy screamed after him. “I know you did!”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89RO"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89RP">The gunslinger, not replying, carefully put the bow in front of the T-post rising out of the handcar’s floor, out of harm’s way.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89RQ"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89RR">The boy’s fists were clenched, his features drawn in agony.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89RS"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89RT"><span class="italic" aid="F89RU">How easily you bluff this young boy,</span> the gunslinger told himself. <span class="italic" aid="F89RV">Again and again his wonderful intuition—his touch—has led him to this point, and again and again you have led him on past it. And how difficult could it be—after all, he has no friends but you.</span></span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89S0"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89S1">In a sudden, simple thought (almost a vision) it came to him that all he had to do was give it over, turn around, take the boy with him, and make him the center of a new force. The Tower did not have to be obtained in this humiliating, nose-rubbing way, did it? Let his quest resume after the boy had a growth of years, when the two of them could cast the man in black aside like a cheap wind-up toy.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89S2"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89S3"><span class="italic" aid="F89S4">Surely,</span> he thought cynically. <span class="italic" aid="F89S5">Surely.</span></span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89S6"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89S7">He knew with sudden coldness that turning backward would mean death for both of them—death or worse: entombment with the Slow Muties behind them. Decay of all the faculties. With, perhaps, the guns of his father living long after both of them, kept in rotten splendor as totems not unlike the unforgotten gas pump.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89S8"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89S9"><span class="italic" aid="F89SA">Show some guts,</span> he told himself falsely.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89SB"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89SC">He reached for the handle and began to pump it. The handcar moved away from the stone piers.</span></p>
<a aid="F89SD"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89SE"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89SF">The boy screamed: <span class="italic" aid="F89SG">“Wait!”</span> And began running on the diagonal, toward where the handcar would emerge nearer the darkness ahead. The gunslinger had an impulse to speed up, to leave the boy alone yet at least with an uncertainty.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89SH"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89SI">Instead, he caught him as he leaped. The heart beneath the thin shirt thrummed and fluttered as Jake clung to him.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89SJ"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89SK">The end was very close now.</span></p>
<div class="calibre_5" aid="F89SL"> </div><h3 class="calibre_8" aid="F89SM"><span class="calibre9" aid="F89SN"><span class="bold1" aid="F89SO">XIII</span></span></h3><div class="calibre_1" aid="F89SP"> </div>
<p class="calibre_9" aid="F89SQ"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89SR">The sound of the river had become very loud, filling even their dreams with its thunder. The gunslinger, more as a whim than anything else, let the boy pump them ahead while he shot a number of the bad arrows, tethered by fine white lengths of thread, into the dark.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89SS"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89ST">The bow was also very bad, incredibly preserved but with a terrible pull and aim despite that, and the gunslinger knew nothing would improve it. Even re-stringing would not help the tired wood. The arrows would not fly far into the dark, but the last one he sent out came back wet and slick. The gunslinger only shrugged when the boy asked him how far to the water, but privately he didn’t think the arrow could have traveled more than sixty yards from the rotted bow—and lucky to get that far.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89SU"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89SV">And still the river’s thunder grew louder, closer.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89T0"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89T1">During the third waking period after the station, a spectral radiance began to grow again. They had entered a long tunnel of some weird phosphorescent rock, and the wet walls glittered and twinkled with thousands of minute starbursts. The boy called them <span class="italic" aid="F89T2">fot-suls.</span> They saw things in a kind of eerie, horror-house surreality.</span></p>
<a aid="F89T3"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89T4"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89T5">The brute sound of the river was channeled to them by the confining rock, magnified in its own natural amplifier. Yet the sound remained oddly constant, even as they approached the crossing point the gunslinger was sure lay ahead, because the walls were widening, drawing back. The angle of their ascent became more pronounced.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89T6"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89T7">The tracks arrowed through the new light. To the gunslinger the clumps of <span class="italic" aid="F89T8">fot-suls</span> looked like the captive tubes of swamp gas sometimes sold for a pretty at the Feast of Reaptide fair; to the boy they looked like endless streamers of neon tubing. But in its glow they could both see that the rock that had enclosed them so long ended up ahead in ragged twin peninsulas that pointed toward a gulf of darkness—the chasm over the river.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89T9"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89TA">The tracks continued out and over that unknowable drop, supported by a trestle aeons old. And beyond, what seemed an incredible distance, was a tiny pinprick of light, not phosphorescence or fluorescence, but the hard, true light of day. It was as tiny as a needle-prick in a dark cloth, yet weighted with frightful meaning.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89TB"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89TC">“Stop,” the boy said. “Stop for a minute. Please.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89TD"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89TE">Unquestioning, the gunslinger let the handcar coast to a stop. The sound of the river was a steady, booming roar, coming from beneath and ahead. The artificial glow from the wet rock was suddenly hateful. For the first time he felt a claustrophobic hand touch him, and the urge to get out, to get free of this living burial, was strong and nearly undeniable.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89TF"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89TG">“We’ll go on,” the boy said. “Is that what he wants? For us to drive the handcar out over . . . <span class="italic" aid="F89TH">that</span> . . . and fall down?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89TI"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89TJ">The gunslinger knew it was not but said: “I don’t know what he wants.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89TK"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89TL">They got down and approached the lip of the drop carefully. <a aid="F89TM"></a>The stone beneath their feet continued to rise until, with a sudden, angling drop, the floor fell away from the tracks and the tracks continued alone, across blackness.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89TN"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89TO">The gunslinger dropped to his knees and peered down. He could dimly make out a complex, nearly incredible webwork of steel girders and struts, disappearing down toward the roar of the river, all in support of the graceful arch of the tracks across the void.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89TP"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89TQ">In his mind’s eye he could imagine the work of time and water on the steel, in deadly tandem. How much support was left? Little? Hardly any? None? He suddenly saw the face of the mummy again, and the way the flesh, seemingly solid, had crumbled to powder at the effortless touch of his finger.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89TR"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89TS">“We’ll walk now,” the gunslinger said.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89TT"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89TU">He half expected the boy to balk again, but he preceded the gunslinger out onto the rails, crossing on the welded steel slats calmly, with sure feet. The gunslinger followed him out over the chasm, ready to catch him if Jake should put a foot wrong.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89TV"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89U0">The gunslinger felt a fine slick of sweat cover his skin. The trestle was rotten, very rotten. It thrummed beneath his feet with the heady motion of the river far beneath, swaying a little on unseen guy wires. <span class="italic" aid="F89U1">We’re acrobats,</span> he thought. <span class="italic" aid="F89U2">Look, Mother, no net. I’m flying.</span></span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89U3"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89U4">He knelt once and examined the crossties they were walking on. They were caked and pitted with rust (he could feel the reason on his face—fresh air, the friend of corruption; they must be very close to the surface now), and a strong blow of the fist made the metal quiver sickly. Once he heard a warning groan beneath his feet and felt the steel settle preparatory to giving way, but he had already moved on.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89U5"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89U6">The boy, of course, was over a hundred pounds lighter and safe enough, unless the going became progressively worse.</span></p>
<a aid="F89U7"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89U8"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89U9">Behind them, the handcar had melted into the general gloom. The stone pier on the left extended out perhaps twenty yards. It jutted further than the one on the right, but this was also left behind and then they were alone over the gulf.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89UA"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89UB">At first it seemed that the tiny prick of daylight remained mockingly constant (perhaps even drawing away from them at the exact pace they approached it—that would be a fine bit of magic indeed), but gradually the gunslinger realized that it was widening, becoming more defined. They were still below it, but the tracks were rising to meet it.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89UC"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89UD">The boy gave a surprised grunt and suddenly lurched to the side, arms pinwheeling in slow, wide revolutions. It seemed that he tottered on the brink for a very long time indeed before stepping forward again.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89UE"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89UF">“It almost went on me,” he said softly, without emotion. “There’s a hole. Step over if you don’t want to take a quick trip to the bottom. Simon says take one giant step.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89UG"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89UH">That was a game the gunslinger knew as Mother Says, remembered well from childhood games with Cuthbert, Jamie, and Alain, but he said nothing, only stepped over.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89UI"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89UJ">“Go back,” Jake said, unsmiling. “You forgot to say ‘May I?’ ”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89UK"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89UL">“Cry your pardon, but I think not.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89UM"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89UN">The crosstie the boy had stepped on had given way almost entirely and flopped downward lazily, swinging on a rotten rivet.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89UO"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89UP">Upward, still upward. It was a nightmare walk and so seemed to go on much longer than it did; the air itself seemed to thicken and become like taffy, and the gunslinger felt as if he might be swimming rather than walking. Again and again his mind tried to turn itself to thoughtful, lunatic consideration of the awful space between this trestle and the river below. His brain viewed it in spectacular detail, and how it would be: the scream of twisting, <a id="filepos509639" aid="F89UQ"></a>giving metal, the lurch as his body slid off to the side, the grabbing for nonexistent handholds with the fingers, the swift rattle of bootheels on treacherous, rotted steel—and then down, turning over and over, the warm spray in his crotch as his bladder let go, the rush of wind against his face, rippling his hair up in a caricature of fright, pulling his eyelids back, the dark water rushing to meet him, faster, outstripping even his own scream—</span></p>
<p class="calibre_" aid="F89UR"><a href="kindle:pos:fid:0003:off:000000003Q" aid="F89US"><img alt="thegunsling_202.jpg" class="calibre13" src="kindle:embed:000E?mime=image/jpeg"/></a></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89UT"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89UU">Metal screamed beneath him and he stepped past it unhurriedly, shifting his weight, at that crucial moment not thinking of the drop, or of how far they had come, or of how far might be left. Not thinking that the boy was expendable and that the sale of his honor was now, at last, nearly negotiated. What a relief it would be when the deal was done!</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89UV"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89V0">“Three ties out,” the boy said coolly. “I’m gonna jump. Here! Right here! <span class="italic" aid="F89V1">Geronimo!</span>”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89V2"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89V3">The gunslinger saw him silhouetted for a moment against the daylight, an awkward, hunched spread-eagle, arms out as if, should all else fail, there was the possibility of flight. He landed and the whole edifice swayed drunkenly under his weight. Metal beneath them protested and something far below fell, first with a crash, then with a splash.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89V4"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89V5">“Are you over?” the gunslinger asked.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89V6"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89V7">“Yar,” the boy said, “but it’s very rotten. Like the ideas of certain people, maybe. I don’t think it will hold you any further than where you are now. Me, but not you. Go back. Go back now and leave me alone.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89V8"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89V9">His voice was cold, but there was hysteria underneath, beating as his heart had beat when he jumped back onto the handcar and Roland had caught him.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89VA"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89VB">The gunslinger stepped over the break. One large step did it. One giant step. <span class="italic" aid="F89VC">Mother, may I? Yes-you-may.</span> The boy was shuddering helplessly. “Go back. I don’t want you to kill me.”</span></p>
<a aid="F89VD"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89VE"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89VF">“For love of the Man Jesus, <span class="italic" aid="F89VG">walk,</span>” the gunslinger said roughly. “It’s going to fall down for sure if we stand here palavering.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89VH"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89VI">The boy walked drunkenly now, his hands held out shudderingly before him, fingers splayed.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89VJ"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89VK">They went up.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89VL"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89VM">Yes, it was much more rotten now. There were frequent breaks of one, two, even three ties, and the gunslinger expected again and again that they would find the long empty space between rails that would either force them back or make them walk on the rails themselves, balanced giddily over the chasm.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89VN"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89VO">He kept his eyes fixed on the daylight.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89VP"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89VQ">The glow had taken on a color—blue—and as it came closer it became softer, paling the radiance of the <span class="italic" aid="F89VR">fot-suls.</span> Fifty yards or a hundred still to cover? He could not say.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89VS"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89VT">They walked, and now he looked at his feet, crossing from tie to tie. When he looked up again, the glow ahead had grown to a hole, and it was not just light but a way out. They were almost there.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F89VU"><span class="calibre3" aid="F89VV">Thirty yards now. No more than that. Ninety short feet. It could be done. Perhaps they would have the man in black yet. Perhaps, in the bright sunlight the evil flowers in his mind would shrivel and anything would be possible.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A00"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A01">The sunlight was blocked out.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A02"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A03">He looked up, startled, peering like a mole from its hole, and saw a silhouette filling the light, eating it up, allowing only chinks of mocking blue around the outline of shoulders and the fork of crotch.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A04"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A05">“Hello, boys!”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A06"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A07">The man in black’s voice echoed to them, amplified in this natural throat of stone, the sarcasm of his good cheer taking on mighty overtones. Blindly, the gunslinger sought the jawbone, but it was gone, lost somewhere, used up.</span></p>
<a aid="F8A08"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A09"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A0A">He laughed above them and the sound crashed around them, reverberating like surf in a filling cave. The boy screamed and tottered, a windmill again, arms gyrating through the scant air.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A0B"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A0C">Metal ripped and sloughed beneath them; the rails canted through a slow and dreamy twisting. The boy plunged, and one hand flew up like a gull in the darkness, up, up, and then he hung over the pit; he dangled there, his dark eyes staring up at the gunslinger in final blind lost knowledge.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A0D"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A0E">“Help me.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A0F"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A0G">Booming, racketing: “No more games. Come now, gunslinger. Or catch me never.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A0H"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A0I">All the chips on the table. Every card up but one. The boy dangled, a living Tarot card, the Hanged Man, the Phoenician sailor, innocent lost and barely above the wave of a stygian sea.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A0J"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A0K"><span class="italic" aid="F8A0L">Wait then, wait awhile.</span></span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A0M"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A0N">“Do I go?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A0O"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A0P"><span class="italic" aid="F8A0Q">His voice is so loud, he makes it hard to think.</span></span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A0R"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A0S">“Help me. Help me, Roland.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A0T"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A0U">The trestle had begun to twist further, screaming, pulling loose from itself, giving—</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A0V"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A10">“Then I shall leave you.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A11"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A12"><span class="italic" aid="F8A13">“No! You shall NOT!”</span></span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A14"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A15">The gunslinger’s legs carried him in a sudden leap, breaking the paralysis that held him; he took a true giant’s step above the dangling boy and landed in a skidding, plunging rush toward the light that offered the Tower frozen on his mind’s eye in a black still life . . .</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A16"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A17">Into sudden silence.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A18"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A19">The silhouette was gone, even the beat of his heart was gone as the trestle settled further, beginning its final slow dance to the depths, tearing loose, his hand finding the rocky, lighted lip of <a aid="F8A1A"></a>damnation; and behind him, in the dreadful silence, the boy spoke from too far beneath him.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A1B"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A1C">“Go then. There are other worlds than these.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A1D"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A1E">Then the trestle tore away, the whole weight of it; and as the gunslinger pulled himself up and through to the light and the breeze and the reality of a new ka, he twisted his head back, for a moment in his agony striving to be Janus—but there was nothing, only plummeting silence, for the boy made no cry as he fell.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A1F"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A1G">Then Roland was up, pulling himself onto the rocky escarpment that looked toward a grassy plain, toward where the man in black stood spread-legged, with arms crossed.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A1H"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A1I">The gunslinger stood drunkenly, pallid as a ghost, eyes huge and swimming beneath his forehead, shirt smeared with the white dust of his final, lunging crawl. It came to him that there would be further degradations of the spirit ahead that might make this one seem infinitesimal, and yet he would still flee it, down corridors and through cities, from bed to bed; he would flee the boy’s face and try to bury it in cunts and killing, only to enter one final room and find it looking at him over a candle flame. He had become the boy; the boy had become him. He was become a werewolf of his own making. In deep dreams he would become the boy and speak the boy’s strange city tongue.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A1J"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A1K"><span class="italic" aid="F8A1L">This is death. Is it? Is it?</span></span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A1M"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A1N">He walked slowly, drunkenly down the rocky hill toward where the man in black waited. Here the tracks had been worn away, under the sun of reason, and it was as if they had never been.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A1O"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A1P">The man in black pushed his hood away with the backs of both hands, laughing.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A1Q"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A1R">“So!” he cried. “Not an end, but the end of the beginning, eh? You progress, gunslinger! You progress! Oh, how I admire you!”</span></p>
<a aid="F8A1S"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A1T"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A1U">The gunslinger drew with blinding speed and fired twelve times. The gunflashes dimmed the sun itself, and the pounding of the explosions slammed back from the rock-faced escarpments behind them.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A1V"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A20">“Now-now,” the man in black said, laughing. “Oh, now-now- <span class="italic" aid="F8A21">now</span>. We make great magic together, you and I. You kill me no more than you kill yourself.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A22"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A23">He withdrew, walking backwards, facing the gunslinger, grinning and beckoning. “Come. Come. Come. Mother, may I? Yes-you-may.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="F8A24"><span class="calibre3" aid="F8A25">The gunslinger followed him in broken boots to the place of counseling.</span></p><p class="calibre10" aid="F8A26"> </p>
<p class="calibre_" aid="F8A27"><img alt="thegunsling_236_0.jpg" class="calibre13" src="kindle:embed:000G?mime=image/jpeg"/></p>
<a aid="F8A28"></a>
