<h1 class="calibre_12" id="calibre_pb_32" aid="G6PI1"><span class="calibre11" aid="G6PI2"><a class="calibre6" href="kindle:pos:fid:002R:off:00000003KD" id="filepos520917" aid="G6PI3"><span class="bold1" aid="G6PI4">The</span><br class="calibre7"/><span class="calibre6" aid="G6PI5"><span class="calibre12" aid="G6PI6"><span class="bold1" aid="G6PI7">GUNSLINGER AND</span></span></span><br class="calibre7"/><span class="calibre6" aid="G6PI8"><span class="calibre12" aid="G6PI9"><span class="bold1" aid="G6PIA">THE MAN IN BLACK</span></span></span></a></span></h1><p class="calibre10" aid="G6PIB"> </p>
<p class="calibre_" aid="G6PIC"><img alt="thegunsling_237_0.jpg" class="calibre13" src="kindle:embed:000H?mime=image/jpeg"/></p>
<a aid="G6PID"></a><a aid="G6PIE"></a>
<div class="mbp_pagebreak" id="calibre_pb_33" aid="G6PIF"></div>
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<html xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml">
  <head>
    <title>The Gunslinger</title>
    <meta content="text/html; charset=utf-8" http-equiv="Content-Type"/>
  <link href="kindle:flow:0001?mime=text/css" rel="stylesheet" type="text/css"/>
<link href="kindle:flow:0002?mime=text/css" rel="stylesheet" type="text/css"/>
</head>
  <body class="calibre" aid="H5A40">
</body>
</html>
<h2 class="calibre_4" id="calibre_pb_35" aid="H5A41"><span class="calibre5" aid="H5A42"><a class="calibre6" href="kindle:pos:fid:002R:off:000000040T" id="filepos521367" aid="H5A43"><span class="bold1" aid="H5A44">CHAPTER FIVE</span><br class="calibre7"/><br class="calibre7"/><span class="calibre6" aid="H5A45"><span class="calibre15" aid="H5A46"><span class="bold1" aid="H5A47">The Gunslinger and the Man in Black</span></span></span></a></span></h2><div class="calibre_1" aid="H5A48"> </div>
<div class="calibre_5" aid="H5A49"> </div><h3 class="calibre_8" aid="H5A4A"><span class="calibre9" aid="H5A4B"><span class="bold1" aid="H5A4C">I</span></span></h3><div class="calibre_1" aid="H5A4D"> </div>
<p class="calibre_9" aid="H5A4E"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A4F">The man in black led him to an ancient killing ground to make palaver. The gunslinger knew it immediately: a golgotha, place-of-the-skull. And bleached skulls stared blandly up at them—cattle, coyotes, deer, rabbits, bumbler. Here the alabaster xylophone of a hen pheasant killed as she fed; there the tiny, delicate bones of a mole, perhaps killed for pleasure by a wild dog.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A4G"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A4H">The golgotha was a bowl indented into the descending slope of the mountain, and below, in easier altitudes, the gunslinger could see Joshua trees and scrub firs. The sky overhead was a softer blue than he had seen for a twelve-month, and there was an indefinable something that spoke of the sea in the not-too-great distance.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A4I"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A4J"><span class="italic" aid="H5A4K">I am in the West, Cuthbert,</span> he thought wonderingly. <span class="italic" aid="H5A4L">If this is not Mid-World, it’s close by.</span></span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A4M"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A4N">The man in black sat on an ancient ironwood log. His boots were powdered white with dust and the uneasy bonemeal of this place. He had put his hood up again, but the gunslinger could see the square shape of his chin clearly, and the shading of his jaw.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A4O"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A4P">The shadowed lips twitched in a smile. “Gather wood, gunslinger. This side of the mountains is gentle, but at this altitude, <a aid="H5A4Q"></a>the cold still may put a knife in one’s belly. And this is a place of death, eh?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A4R"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A4S">“I’ll kill you,” the gunslinger said.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A4T"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A4U">“No you won’t. You can’t. But you can gather wood to remember your Isaac.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A4V"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A50">The gunslinger had no understanding of the reference. He went wordlessly and gathered wood like a common cook’s boy. The pickings were slim. There was no devil-grass on this side and the ironwood would not burn. It had become stone. He returned finally with a large armload of likely sticks, powdered and dusted with disintegrated bone, as if dipped in flour. The sun had sunk beyond the highest Joshua trees and had taken on a reddish glow. It peered at them with baleful indifference.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A51"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A52">“Excellent,” the man in black said. “How exceptional you are! How methodical! How resourceful! I salute you!” He giggled, and the gunslinger dropped the wood at his feet with a crash that ballooned up bone dust.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A53"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A54">The man in black did not start or jump; he merely began laying the fire. The gunslinger watched, fascinated, as the ideogram (fresh, this time) took shape. When it was finished, it resembled a small and complex double chimney about two feet high. The man in black lifted his hand skyward, shaking back the voluminous sleeve from a tapered, handsome hand, and brought it down rapidly, index and pinky fingers forked out in the traditional sign of the evil eye. There was a blue flash of flame, and their fire was lighted.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A55"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A56">“I have matches,” the man in black said jovially, “but I thought you might enjoy the magic. For a pretty, gunslinger. Now cook our dinner.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A57"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A58">The folds of his robe shivered, and the plucked and gutted carcass of a plump rabbit fell on the dirt.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A59"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A5A">The gunslinger spitted the rabbit wordlessly and roasted it. A savory smell drifted up as the sun went down. Purple shadows <a aid="H5A5B"></a>drifted hungrily over the bowl where the man in black had chosen to finally face him. The gunslinger felt hunger begin to rumble endlessly in his belly as the rabbit browned; but when the meat was cooked and its juices sealed in, he handed the entire skewer wordlessly to the man in black, rummaged in his own nearly flat knapsack, and withdrew the last of his jerky. It was salty, painful to his mouth, and tasted like tears.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A5C"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A5D">“That’s a worthless gesture,” the man in black said, managing to sound angry and amused at the same time.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A5E"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A5F">“Nevertheless,” the gunslinger said. There were tiny sores in his mouth, the result of vitamin deprivation, and the salt taste made him grin bitterly.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A5G"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A5H">“Are you afraid of enchanted meat?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A5I"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A5J">“Yes indeed.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A5K"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A5L">The man in black slipped his hood back.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A5M"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A5N">The gunslinger looked at him silently. In a way, the face that the hood had hidden was an uneasy disappointment. It was handsome and regular, with none of the marks and twists which indicate a man who has been through awesome times and has been privy to great secrets. His hair was black and of a ragged, matted length. His forehead was high, his eyes dark and brilliant. His nose was nondescript. The lips were full and sensual. His complexion was pallid, as was the gunslinger’s own.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A5O"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A5P">The gunslinger said finally, “I expected an older man.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A5Q"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A5R">“Why? I am nearly immortal, as are you, Roland—for now, at least. I could have taken a face with which you would have been more familiar, but I elected to show you the one I was—ah—born with. See, gunslinger, the sunset.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A5S"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A5T">The sun had departed already, and the western sky was filled with sullen furnace light.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A5U"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A5V">“You won’t see another sunrise for what may seem a very long time,” the man in black said.</span></p>
<a aid="H5A60"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A61"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A62">The gunslinger remembered the pit under the mountains and then looked at the sky, where the constellations sprawled in clockspring profusion.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A63"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A64">“It doesn’t matter,” he said softly, “now.”</span></p>
<div class="calibre_5" aid="H5A65"> </div><h3 class="calibre_8" aid="H5A66"><span class="calibre9" aid="H5A67"><span class="bold1" aid="H5A68">II</span></span></h3><div class="calibre_1" aid="H5A69"> </div>
<p class="calibre_9" aid="H5A6A"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A6B">The man in black shuffled the cards with flying hands. The deck was huge, the designs on the back convoluted. “These are Tarot cards, gunslinger—of a sort. A mixture of the standard deck to which have been added a selection of my own development. Now watch carefully.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A6C"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A6D">“What will I watch?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A6E"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A6F">“I’m going to tell your future. Seven cards must be turned, one at a time, and placed in conjunction with the others. I’ve not done this since the days when Gilead stood and the ladies played at Points on the west lawn. And I suspect I’ve <span class="italic" aid="H5A6G">never</span> read a tale such as yours.” Mockery was creeping into his voice again. “You are the world’s last adventurer. The last crusader. How that must please you, Roland! Yet you have no idea how close you stand to the Tower now, as you resume your quest. Worlds turn about your head.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A6H"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A6I">“What do you mean, resume? I never left off.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A6J"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A6K">At this the man in black laughed heartily, but would not say what he found so funny. “Read my fortune then,” Roland said harshly.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A6L"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A6M">The first card was turned.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A6N"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A6O">“The Hanged Man,” the man in black said. The darkness had given him back his hood. “Yet here, in conjunction with nothing else, it signifies strength, not death. You, gunslinger, are the <a aid="H5A6P"></a>Hanged Man, plodding ever onward toward your goal over the pits of Na’ar. You’ve already dropped one co-traveler into that pit, have you not?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A6Q"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A6R">The gunslinger said nothing, and the second card was turned.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A6S"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A6T">“The Sailor! Note the clear brow, the hairless cheeks, the wounded eyes. He drowns, gunslinger, and no one throws out the line. The boy Jake.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A6U"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A6V">The gunslinger winced, said nothing.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A70"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A71">The third card was turned. A baboon stood grinningly astride a young man’s shoulder. The young man’s face was turned up, a grimace of stylized dread and horror on his features. Looking more closely, the gunslinger saw the baboon held a whip.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A72"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A73">“The Prisoner,” the man in black said. The fire cast uneasy, flickering shadows over the face of the ridden man, making it seem to move and writhe in wordless terror. The gunslinger flicked his eyes away.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A74"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A75">“A trifle upsetting, isn’t he?” the man in black said, and seemed on the verge of sniggering.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A76"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A77">He turned the fourth card. A woman with a shawl over her head sat spinning at a wheel. To the gunslinger’s dazed eyes, she appeared to be smiling craftily and sobbing at the same time.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A78"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A79">“The Lady of the Shadows,” the man in black remarked. “Does she look two-faced to you, gunslinger? She is. Two faces at least. She broke the blue plate!”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A7A"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A7B">“What do you mean?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A7C"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A7D">“I don’t know.” And—in this case, at least—the gunslinger thought his adversary was telling the truth.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A7E"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A7F">“Why are you showing me these?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A7G"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A7H">“Don’t ask!” the man in black said sharply, yet he smiled. “Don’t ask. Merely watch. Consider this only pointless ritual if it eases you and cools you to do so. Like church.”</span></p>
<a aid="H5A7I"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A7J"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A7K">He tittered and turned the fifth card.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A7L"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A7M">A grinning reaper clutched a scythe with bony fingers. “Death,” the man in black said simply. “Yet not for you.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A7N"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A7O">The sixth card.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A7P"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A7Q">The gunslinger looked at it and felt a strange, crawling anticipation in his guts. The feeling was mixed with horror and joy, and the whole of the emotion was unnameable. It made him feel like throwing up and dancing at the same time.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A7R"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A7S">“The Tower,” the man in black said softly. “Here is the Tower.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A7T"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A7U">The gunslinger’s card occupied the center of the pattern; each of the following four stood at one corner, like satellites circling a star.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A7V"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A80">“Where does that one go?” the gunslinger asked.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A81"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A82">The man in black placed the Tower over the Hanged Man, covering it completely.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A83"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A84">“What does that mean?” the gunslinger asked.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A85"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A86">The man in black did not answer.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A87"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A88">“What does that mean?” he asked raggedly.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A89"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A8A">The man in black did not answer.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A8B"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A8C">“Goddamn you!”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A8D"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A8E">No answer.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A8F"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A8G">“Then be damned to you. What’s the seventh card?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A8H"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A8I">The man in black turned the seventh. A sun rose in a luminously blue sky. Cupids and sprites sported around it. Below the sun was a great red field upon which it shone. Roses or blood? The gunslinger could not tell. <span class="italic" aid="H5A8J">Perhaps,</span> he thought, <span class="italic" aid="H5A8K">it’s both.</span></span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A8L"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A8M">“The seventh card is Life,” the man in black said softly. “But not for you.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A8N"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A8O">“Where does it fit the pattern?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A8P"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A8Q">“That is not for you to know now,” the man in black said. “Or for me to know. I’m not the great one you seek, Roland. I am <a aid="H5A8R"></a>merely his emissary.” He flipped the card carelessly into the dying fire. It charred, curled, and flashed to flame. The gunslinger felt his heart quail and turn icy in his chest.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A8S"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A8T">“Sleep now,” the man in black said carelessly. “Perchance to dream and that sort of thing.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A8U"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A8V">“What my bullets won’t do, mayhap my hands will,” the gunslinger said. His legs coiled with savage, splendid suddenness, and he flew across the fire at the other, arms outstretched. The man in black, smiling, swelled in his vision and then retreated down a long and echoing corridor. The world filled with the sound of sardonic laughter, he was falling, dying, sleeping.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A90"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A91">He dreamed.</span></p>
<div class="calibre_5" aid="H5A92"> </div><h3 class="calibre_8" aid="H5A93"><span class="calibre9" aid="H5A94"><span class="bold1" aid="H5A95">III</span></span></h3><div class="calibre_1" aid="H5A96"> </div>
<p class="calibre_9" aid="H5A97"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A98">The universe was void. Nothing moved. Nothing was.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A99"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A9A">The gunslinger drifted, bemused.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A9B"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A9C">“Let’s have a little light,” the voice of the man in black said nonchalantly, and there was light. The gunslinger thought in a detached way that light was pretty good.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A9D"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A9E">“Now darkness overhead with stars in it. Water down below.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A9F"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A9G">It happened. He drifted over endless seas. Above, the stars twinkled endlessly, yet he saw none of the constellations which had guided him across his long life.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A9H"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A9I">“Land,” the man in black invited, and there was; it heaved itself out of the water in endless, galvanic convulsions. It was red, arid, cracked and glazed with sterility. Volcanoes blurted endless magma like giant pimples on some ugly adolescent’s baseball head.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A9J"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A9K">“Okay,” the man in black was saying. “That’s a start. Let’s have some plants. Trees. Grass and fields.”</span></p>
<a aid="H5A9L"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A9M"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A9N">There was. Dinosaurs rambled here and there, growling and whoofing and eating each other and getting stuck in bubbling, odiferous tarpits. Huge tropical rain-forests sprawled everywhere. Giant ferns waved at the sky with serrated leaves. Beetles with two heads crawled on some of them. All this the gunslinger saw. And yet he felt big.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A9O"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A9P">“Now bring man,” the man in black said softly, but the gunslinger was falling . . . falling up. The horizon of this vast and fecund earth began to curve. Yes, they had all said it curved, his teacher Vannay had claimed it had been proved long before the world had moved on. But this—</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A9Q"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A9R">Further and further, higher and higher. Continents took shape before his amazed eyes, and were obscured with clocksprings of clouds. The world’s atmosphere held it in a placental sac. And the sun, rising beyond the earth’s shoulder—</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A9S"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A9T">He cried out and threw an arm before his eyes.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5A9U"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5A9V">“Let there be light!”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AA0"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AA1">The voice no longer belonged to the man in black. It was gigantic, echoing. It filled space, and the spaces between space.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AA2"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AA3"><span class="italic" aid="H5AA4">“Light!”</span></span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AA5"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AA6">Falling, falling.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AA7"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AA8">The sun shrank. A red planet stamped with canals whirled past him, two moons circling it furiously. Beyond this was a whirling belt of stones and a gigantic planet that seethed with gases, too huge to support itself, oblate in consequence. Further out was a ringed world that glittered like a precious gem within its engirdlement of icy spicules.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AA9"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AAA"><span class="italic" aid="H5AAB">“Light! Let there be—”</span></span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AAC"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AAD">Other worlds, one, two, three. Far beyond the last, one lonely ball of ice and rock twirled in dead darkness about a sun that glittered no brighter than a tarnished penny.</span></p>
<a aid="H5AAE"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AAF"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AAG">Beyond this, darkness.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AAH"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AAI">“No,” the gunslinger said, and his word on it was flat and echoless in the black. It was darker than dark, blacker than black. Beside this, the darkest night of a man’s soul was as noonday, the darkness under the mountains a mere smudge on the face of Light. “No more. Please, no more now. No more—”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AAJ"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AAK">“LIGHT!”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AAL"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AAM">“No more. No more, please—”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AAN"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AAO">The stars themselves began to shrink. Whole nebulae drew together and became glowing smudges. The whole universe seemed to be drawing around him.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AAP"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AAQ">“Please no more no more no more—”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AAR"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AAS">The voice of the man in black whispered silkily in his ear: “Then renege. Cast away all thoughts of the Tower. Go your way, gunslinger, and begin the long job of saving your soul.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AAT"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AAU">He gathered himself. Shaken and alone, enwrapt in the darkness, terrified of an ultimate meaning rushing at him, he gathered himself and uttered the final answer on that subject:</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AAV"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AB0">“NEVER!”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AB1"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AB2"><span class="bold" aid="H5AB3">“THEN LET THERE BE LIGHT!”</span></span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AB4"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AB5">And there <span class="italic" aid="H5AB6">was</span> light, crashing in on him like a hammer, a great and primordial light. Consciousness had no chance of survival in that great glare, but before it perished, the gunslinger saw something clearly, something he believed to be of cosmic importance. He clutched it with agonized effort and then went deep, seeking refuge in himself before that light should blind his eyes and blast his sanity.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AB7"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AB8">He fled the light and the knowledge the light implied, and so came back to himself. Even so do the rest of us; even so the best of us.</span></p>
<a aid="H5AB9"></a>
<div class="calibre_5" aid="H5ABA"> </div><h3 class="calibre_8" aid="H5ABB"><span class="calibre9" aid="H5ABC"><span class="bold1" aid="H5ABD">IV</span></span></h3><div class="calibre_1" aid="H5ABE"> </div>
<p class="calibre_9" aid="H5ABF"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ABG">It was still night—whether the same or another, he had no immediate way of knowing. He pushed himself up from where his demon spring at the man in black had carried him and looked at the ironwood where Walter o’ Dim (as some along Roland’s way had named him) had been sitting. He was gone.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ABH"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ABI">A great sense of despair flooded him—God, all that to do over again—and then the man in black said from behind him: “Over here, gunslinger. I don’t like you so close. You talk in your sleep.” He tittered.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ABJ"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ABK">The gunslinger got groggily to his knees and turned around. The fire had burned down to red embers and gray ashes, leaving the familiar decayed pattern of exhausted fuel. The man in black was seated next to it, smacking his lips with unlovely enthusiasm over the greasy remains of the rabbit.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ABL"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ABM">“You did fairly well,” the man in black said. “I never could have sent that vision to your father. He would have come back drooling.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ABN"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ABO">“What was it?” the gunslinger asked. His words were blurred and shaky. He felt that if he tried to rise, his legs would buckle.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ABP"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ABQ">“The universe,” the man in black said carelessly. He burped and threw the bones into the fire where they first glistened and then blackened. The wind above the cup of the golgotha keened and moaned.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ABR"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ABS">“Universe?” the gunslinger said blankly. It was a word with which he was unfamiliar. His first thought was that the other was speaking poetry.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ABT"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ABU">“You want the Tower,” the man in black said. It seemed to be a question.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ABV"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AC0">“Yes.”</span></p>
<a aid="H5AC1"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AC2"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AC3">“Well, you shan’t have it,” the man in black said, and smiled with bright cruelty. “No one cares in the counsels of the great if you pawn your soul or sell it outright, Roland. I have an idea of how close to the edge that last pushed you. The Tower will kill you half a world away.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AC4"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AC5">“You know nothing of me,” the gunslinger said quietly, and the smile faded from the other’s lips.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AC6"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AC7">“I made your father and I broke him,” the man in black said grimly. “I came to your mother as Marten—there’s a truth you always suspected, is it not?—and took her. She bent beneath me like a willow . . . although (this may comfort you) she never broke. In any case it was written, and it was. I am the furthest minion of he who now rules the Dark Tower, and Earth has been given into that king’s red hand.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AC8"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AC9">“Red? Why do you say red?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ACA"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ACB">“Never mind. We’ll not speak of him, although you’ll learn more than you cared to if you press on. What hurt you once will hurt you twice. This is not the beginning but the beginning’s end. You’d do well to remember that . . . but you never do.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ACC"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ACD">“I don’t understand.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ACE"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ACF">“No. You don’t. You never did. You never will. You have no imagination. You’re blind that way.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ACG"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ACH">“What did I see?” the gunslinger asked. “What did I see at the end? What was it?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ACI"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ACJ">“What did it seem to be?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ACK"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ACL">The gunslinger was silent, thoughtful. He felt for his tobacco, but there was none. The man in black did not offer to refill his poke by either black magic or white. Later he might find more in his grow-bag, but later seemed very far away now.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ACM"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ACN">“There was light,” the gunslinger said finally. “Great white light. And then—” He broke off and stared at the man in black. <a aid="H5ACO"></a>He was leaning forward, and an alien emotion was stamped on his face, writ too large for lies or denial. It was awe or wonder. Perhaps they were the same.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ACP"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ACQ">“You don’t know,” he said, and began to smile. “O great sorcerer who brings the dead to life. You don’t know. You’re a fake!”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ACR"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ACS">“I know,” the man in black said. “But I don’t know . . . what.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ACT"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ACU">“White light,” the gunslinger repeated. “And then—a blade of grass. One single blade of grass that filled everything. And I was tiny. Infinitesimal.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ACV"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AD0">“Grass.” The man in black closed his eyes. His face looked drawn and haggard. “A blade of grass. Are you sure?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AD1"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AD2">“Yes.” The gunslinger frowned. “But it was purple.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AD3"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AD4">“Hear me now, Roland, son of Steven. Would you hear me?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AD5"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AD6">“Yes.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AD7"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AD8">And so the man in black began to speak.</span></p>
<div class="calibre_5" aid="H5AD9"> </div><h3 class="calibre_8" aid="H5ADA"><span class="calibre9" aid="H5ADB"><span class="bold1" aid="H5ADC">V</span></span></h3><div class="calibre_1" aid="H5ADD"> </div>
<p class="calibre_9" aid="H5ADE"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ADF">The universe (he said) is the Great All, and offers a paradox too great for the finite mind to grasp. As the living brain cannot conceive of a nonliving brain—although it may think it can—the finite mind cannot grasp the infinite.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ADG"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ADH">The prosaic fact of the universe’s existence alone defeats both the pragmatist and the romantic. There was a time, yet a hundred generations before the world moved on, when mankind had achieved enough technical and scientific prowess to chip a few splinters from the great stone pillar of reality. Even so, the false light of science (knowledge, if you like) shone in only a few developed countries. One company (or cabal) led the way in this regard; North Central Positronics, it called itself. Yet, despite a <a aid="H5ADI"></a>tremendous increase in available facts, there were remarkably few insights.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ADJ"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ADK">“Gunslinger, our many-times-great grandfathers conquered the-disease-which-rots, which they called cancer, almost conquered aging, walked on the moon—”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ADL"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ADM">“I don’t believe that,” the gunslinger said flatly.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ADN"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ADO">To this the man in black merely smiled and answered, “You needn’t. Yet it was so. They made or discovered a hundred other marvelous baubles. But this wealth of information produced little or no insight. There were no great odes written to the wonders of artificial insemination—having babies from frozen mansperm—or to the cars that ran on power from the sun. Few if any seemed to have grasped the truest principle of reality: new knowledge leads always to yet more awesome mysteries. Greater physiological knowledge of the brain makes the existence of the soul less possible yet more probable by the nature of the search. Do you see? Of course you don’t. You’ve reached the limits of your ability to comprehend. But never mind—that’s beside the point.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ADP"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ADQ">“What <span class="italic" aid="H5ADR">is</span> the point, then?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ADS"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ADT">“The greatest mystery the universe offers is not life but size. Size encompasses life, and the Tower encompasses size. The child, who is most at home with wonder, says: Daddy, what is above the sky? And the father says: The darkness of space. The child: What is beyond space? The father: The galaxy. The child: Beyond the galaxy? The father: Another galaxy. The child: Beyond the other galaxies? The father: No one knows.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ADU"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ADV">“You see? Size defeats us. For the fish, the lake in which he lives is the universe. What does the fish think when he is jerked up by the mouth through the silver limits of existence and into a new universe where the air drowns him and the light is blue <a aid="H5AE0"></a>madness? Where huge bipeds with no gills stuff it into a suffocating box and cover it with wet weeds to die?</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AE1"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AE2">“Or one might take the tip of a pencil and magnify it. One reaches the point where a stunning realization strikes home: The pencil-tip is not solid; it is composed of atoms which whirl and revolve like a trillion demon planets. What seems solid to us is actually only a loose net held together by gravity. Viewed at their actual size, the distances between these atoms might become leagues, gulfs, aeons. The atoms themselves are composed of nuclei and revolving protons and electrons. One may step down further to subatomic particles. And then to what? Tachyons? Nothing? Of course not. Everything in the universe denies nothing; to suggest an ending is the one absurdity.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AE3"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AE4">“If you fell outward to the limit of the universe, would you find a board fence and signs reading DEAD END? No. You might find something hard and rounded, as the chick must see the egg from the inside. And if you should peck through that shell (or find a door), what great and torrential light might shine through your opening at the end of space? Might you look through and discover our entire universe is but part of one atom on a blade of grass? Might you be forced to think that by burning a twig you incinerate an eternity of eternities? That existence rises not to one infinite but to an infinity of them?</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AE5"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AE6">“Perhaps you saw what place our universe plays in the scheme of things—as no more than an atom in a blade of grass. Could it be that everything we can perceive, from the microscopic virus to the distant Horsehead Nebula, is contained in one blade of grass that may have existed for only a single season in an alien time-flow? What if that blade should be cut off by a scythe? When it begins to die, would the rot seep into our own universe and our own lives, turning everything yellow and brown and <a aid="H5AE7"></a>desiccated? Perhaps it’s already begun to happen. We say the world has moved on; maybe we really mean that it has begun to dry up.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AE8"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AE9">“Think how small such a concept of things makes us, gunslinger! If a God watches over it all, does He actually mete out justice for a race of gnats among an infinitude of races of gnats? Does His eye see the sparrow fall when the sparrow is less than a speck of hydrogen floating disconnected in the depth of space? And if He does see . . . what must the nature of such a God be? Where does He live? How is it possible to live beyond infinity?</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AEA"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AEB">“Imagine the sand of the Mohaine Desert, which you crossed to find me, and imagine a trillion universes—not worlds but <span class="italic" aid="H5AEC">universes</span>—encapsulated in each grain of that desert; and within each universe an infinity of others. We tower over these universes from our pitiful grass vantage point; with one swing of your boot you may knock a billion billion worlds flying off into darkness, in a chain never to be completed.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AED"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AEE">“Size, gunslinger . . . <span class="italic" aid="H5AEF">size</span> . . .</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AEG"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AEH">“Yet suppose further. Suppose that all worlds, all universes, met in a single nexus, a single pylon, a Tower. And within it, a stairway, perhaps rising to the Godhead itself. Would you dare climb to the top, gunslinger? Could it be that somewhere above all of endless reality, there exists a Room? . . .</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AEI"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AEJ">“You dare not.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AEK"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AEL">And in the gunslinger’s mind, those words echoed: <span class="italic" aid="H5AEM">You dare not.</span></span></p>
<div class="calibre_5" aid="H5AEN"> </div><h3 class="calibre_8" aid="H5AEO"><span class="calibre9" aid="H5AEP"><span class="bold1" aid="H5AEQ">VI</span></span></h3><div class="calibre_1" aid="H5AER"> </div>
<p class="calibre_9" aid="H5AES"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AET">“Someone has dared,” the gunslinger said.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AEU"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AEV">“Who would that be?”</span></p>
<a aid="H5AF0"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AF1"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AF2">“God,” the gunslinger said softly. His eyes gleamed. “God has dared . . . or the king you spoke of . . . or . . . is the room empty, seer?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AF3"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AF4">“I don’t know.” Fear passed over the man in black’s bland face, as soft and dark as a buzzard’s wing. “And, furthermore, I don’t ask. It might be unwise.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AF5"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AF6">“Afraid of being struck dead?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AF7"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AF8">“Perhaps afraid of . . . an accounting.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AF9"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AFA">The man in black was silent for a while. The night was very long. The Milky Way sprawled above them in great splendor, yet terrifying in the emptiness between its burning lamps. The gunslinger wondered what he would feel if that inky sky should split open and let in a torrent of light.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AFB"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AFC">“The fire,” he said. “I’m cold.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AFD"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AFE">“Build it up yourself,” said the man in black. “It’s the butler’s night off.”</span></p>
<div class="calibre_5" aid="H5AFF"> </div><h3 class="calibre_8" aid="H5AFG"><span class="calibre9" aid="H5AFH"><span class="bold1" aid="H5AFI">VII</span></span></h3><div class="calibre_1" aid="H5AFJ"> </div>
<p class="calibre_9" aid="H5AFK"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AFL">The gunslinger drowsed awhile and awoke to see the man in black regarding him avidly, unhealthily.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AFM"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AFN">“What are you staring at?” An old saying of Cort’s occurred to him. “Do you see your sister’s bum?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AFO"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AFP">“I’m staring at you, of course.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AFQ"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AFR">“Well, don’t.” He poked up the fire, ruining the precision of the ideogram. “I don’t like it.” He looked to the east to see if there was the beginning of light, but this night went on and on.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AFS"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AFT">“You seek the light so soon.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AFU"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AFV">“I was made for light.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AG0"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AG1">“Ah, so you were! And so impolite of me to forget the fact! <a aid="H5AG2"></a>Yet we have much to discuss yet, you and I. For so has it been told to me by my king and master.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AG3"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AG4">“Who is this king?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AG5"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AG6">The man in black smiled. “Shall we tell the truth then, you and I? No more lies?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AG7"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AG8">“I thought we had been.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AG9"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AGA">But the man in black persisted as if Roland hadn’t spoken. “Shall there be truth between us, as two men? Not as friends, but as equals? There is an offer you will get rarely, Roland. Only equals speak the truth, that’s my thought on’t. Friends and lovers lie endlessly, caught in the web of regard. How tiresome!”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AGB"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AGC">“Well, I wouldn’t want to tire you, so let us speak the truth.” He had never spoken less on this night. “Start by telling me what exactly you mean by glammer.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AGD"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AGE">“Why, enchantment, gunslinger! My king’s enchantment has prolonged this night and will prolong it until our palaver is done.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AGF"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AGG">“How long will that be?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AGH"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AGI">“Long. I can tell you no better. I do not know myself.” The man in black stood over the fire, and the glowing embers made patterns on his face. “Ask. I will tell you what I know. You have caught me. It is fair; I did not think you would. Yet your quest has only begun. Ask. It will lead us to business soon enough.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AGJ"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AGK">“Who is your king?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AGL"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AGM">“I have never seen him, but you must. But before you meet him, you must first meet the Ageless Stranger.” The man in black smiled spitelessly. “You must slay him, gunslinger. Yet I think it is not what you wished to ask.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AGN"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AGO">“If you’ve never seen your king and master, how do you know him?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AGP"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AGQ">“He comes to me in dreams. As a stripling he came to me, when I lived, poor and unknown, in a far land. A sheaf of <a aid="H5AGR"></a>centuries ago he imbued me with my duty and promised me my reward, although there were many errands in my youth and the days of my manhood, before my apotheosis. You are that apotheosis, gunslinger. You are my climax.” He tittered. “You see, someone has taken you seriously.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AGS"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AGT">“And this Stranger, does he have a name?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AGU"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AGV">“O, he is named.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AH0"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AH1">“And what is his name?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AH2"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AH3">“Legion,” the man in black said softly, and somewhere in the easterly darkness where the mountains lay, a rockslide punctuated his words and a puma screamed like a woman. The gunslinger shivered and the man in black flinched. “Yet I do not think that is what you wished to ask, either. It is not your nature to think so far ahead.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AH4"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AH5">The gunslinger knew the question; it had gnawed him all this night, and he thought, for years before. It trembled on his lips but he didn’t ask it . . . not yet.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AH6"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AH7">“This Stranger is a minion of the Tower? Like yourself?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AH8"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AH9">“Yar. He <span class="italic" aid="H5AHA">darkles.</span> He <span class="italic" aid="H5AHB">tincts.</span> He is in all times. Yet there is one greater than he.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AHC"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AHD">“Who?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AHE"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AHF">“Ask me no more!” the man in black cried. His voice aspired to sternness and crumbled into beseechment. “I know not! I do not wish to know. To speak of the things in End-World is to speak of the ruination of one’s own soul.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AHG"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AHH">“And beyond the Ageless Stranger is the Tower and whatever the Tower contains?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AHI"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AHJ">“Yes,” whispered the man in black. “But none of these things are what you wish to ask.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AHK"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AHL">True.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AHM"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AHN">“All right,” the gunslinger said, and then asked the world’s oldest question. “Will I succeed? Will I win through?”</span></p>
<a aid="H5AHO"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AHP"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AHQ">“If I answered that question, gunslinger, you’d kill me.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AHR"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AHS">“I <span class="italic" aid="H5AHT">ought</span> to kill you. You need killing.” His hands had dropped to the worn butts of his guns.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AHU"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AHV">“Those do not open doors, gunslinger; those only close them forever.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AI0"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AI1">“Where must I go?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AI2"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AI3">“Start west. Go to the sea. Where the world ends is where you must begin. There was a man who gave you advice . . . the man you bested so long ago—”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AI4"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AI5">“Yes, Cort,” the gunslinger interrupted impatiently.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AI6"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AI7">“The advice was to wait. It was bad advice. For even then my plans against your father had proceeded. He sent you away and when you returned—”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AI8"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AI9">“I’d not hear you speak of that,” the gunslinger said, and in his mind he heard his mother singing: <span class="italic" aid="H5AIA">Baby-bunting, baby dear, baby bring your basket here.</span></span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AIB"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AIC">“Then hear this: when you returned, Marten had gone west, to join the rebels. So all said, anyway, and so you believed. Yet he and a certain witch left you a trap and you fell into it. Good boy! And although Marten was long gone by then, there was a man who sometimes made you think of him, was there not? A man who affected the dress of a monk and the shaven head of a penitent—”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AID"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AIE">“Walter,” the gunslinger whispered. And although he had come so far in his musings, the bald truth still amazed him. “<span class="italic" aid="H5AIF">You.</span> Marten never left at all.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AIG"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AIH">The man in black tittered. “At your service.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AII"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AIJ">“I ought to kill you now.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AIK"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AIL">“That would hardly be fair. Besides, all of that was long ago. Now comes the time of sharing.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AIM"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AIN">“You never left,” the gunslinger repeated, stunned. “You only changed.”</span></p>
<a aid="H5AIO"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AIP"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AIQ">“Sit,” the man in black invited. “I’ll tell you stories, as many as you would hear. Your own stories, I think, will be much longer.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AIR"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AIS">“I don’t talk of myself,” the gunslinger muttered.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AIT"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AIU">“Yet tonight you must. So that we may understand.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AIV"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AJ0">“Understand what? My purpose? You know that. To find the Tower is my purpose. I’m sworn.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AJ1"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AJ2">“Not your purpose, gunslinger. Your mind. Your slow, prodding, tenacious mind. There has never been one quite like it, in all the history of the world. Perhaps in the history of creation.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AJ3"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AJ4">“This is the time of speaking. This is the time of histories.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AJ5"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AJ6">“Then speak.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AJ7"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AJ8">The man in black shook the voluminous arm of his robe. A foil-wrapped package fell out and caught the dying embers in many reflective folds.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AJ9"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AJA">“Tobacco, gunslinger. Would you smoke?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AJB"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AJC">He had been able to resist the rabbit, but he could not resist this. He opened the foil with eager fingers. There was fine crumbled tobacco inside, and green leaves to wrap it in, amazingly moist. He had not seen such tobacco for ten years.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AJD"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AJE">He rolled two cigarettes and bit the ends of each to release the flavor. He offered one to the man in black, who took it. Each of them took a burning twig from the fire.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AJF"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AJG">The gunslinger lit his cigarette and drew the aromatic smoke deep into his lungs, closing his eyes to concentrate the senses. He blew out with long, slow satisfaction.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AJH"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AJI">“Is it good?” the man in black inquired.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AJJ"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AJK">“Yes. Very good.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AJL"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AJM">“Enjoy it. It may be the last smoke for you in a very long time.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AJN"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AJO">The gunslinger took this impassively.</span></p>
<a aid="H5AJP"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AJQ"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AJR">“Very well,” the man in black said. “To begin then:</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AJS"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AJT">“You must understand the Tower has always been, and there have always been boys who know of it and lust for it, more than power or riches or women . . . boys who look for the doors that lead to it . . .”</span></p>
<div class="calibre_5" aid="H5AJU"> </div><h3 class="calibre_8" aid="H5AJV"><span class="calibre9" aid="H5AK0"><span class="bold1" aid="H5AK1">VIII</span></span></h3><div class="calibre_1" aid="H5AK2"> </div>
<p class="calibre_9" aid="H5AK3"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AK4">There was talk then, a night’s worth of talk and God alone knew how much more (or how much was true), but the gunslinger remembered little of it later . . . and to his oddly practical mind, little of it seemed to matter. The man in black told him again that he must go to the sea, which lay no more than twenty easy miles to the west, and there he would be invested with the power of <span class="italic" aid="H5AK5">drawing.</span></span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AK6"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AK7">“But that’s not exactly right, either,” the man in black said, pitching his cigarette into the remains of the campfire. “No one wants to invest you with a power of any kind, gunslinger; it is simply <span class="italic" aid="H5AK8">in</span> you, and I am compelled to tell you, partly because of the sacrifice of the boy, and partly because it is the law; the natural law of things. Water must run downhill, and you must be told. You will draw three, I understand . . . but I don’t really care, and I don’t really want to know.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AK9"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AKA">“The three,” the gunslinger murmured, thinking of the Oracle.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AKB"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AKC">“And then the fun begins! But, by then, I’ll be long gone. Goodbye, gunslinger. My part is done now. The chain is still in your hands. ’Ware it doesn’t wrap itself around your neck.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AKD"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AKE">Compelled by something outside him, Roland said, “You have one more thing to say, don’t you?”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AKF"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AKG">“Yes,” the man in black said, and he smiled at the gunslinger <a aid="H5AKH"></a>with his depthless eyes and stretched one of his hands out toward him. “Let there be light.”</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AKI"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AKJ">And there was light, and this time the light was good.</span></p>
<div class="calibre_5" aid="H5AKK"> </div><h3 class="calibre_8" aid="H5AKL"><span class="calibre9" aid="H5AKM"><span class="bold1" aid="H5AKN">IX</span></span></h3><div class="calibre_1" aid="H5AKO"> </div>
<p class="calibre_9" aid="H5AKP"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AKQ">Roland awoke by the ruins of the campfire to find himself ten years older. His black hair had thinned at the temples and there had gone the gray of cobwebs at the end of autumn. The lines in his face were deeper, his skin rougher.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AKR"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AKS">The remains of the wood he had carried had turned to something like stone, and the man in black was a laughing skeleton in a rotting black robe, more bones in this place of bones, one more skull in this golgotha.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AKT"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AKU"><span class="italic" aid="H5AKV">Or is it really you?</span> he thought. <span class="italic" aid="H5AL0">I have my doubts, Walter o’ Dim . . . I have my doubts, Marten-that-was.</span></span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AL1"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AL2">He stood up and looked around. Then, with a sudden quick gesture, he reached toward the remains of his companion of the night before (if it was indeed the remains of Walter), a night that had somehow lasted ten years. He broke off the grinning jawbone and jammed it carelessly into the left hip pocket of his jeans—a fitting enough replacement for the one lost under the mountains.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AL3"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AL4">“How many lies did you tell me?” he asked. Many, he was sure, but what made them good lies was that they had been mixed with the truth.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AL5"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AL6">The Tower. Somewhere ahead, it waited for him—the nexus of Time, the nexus of Size.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5AL7"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5AL8">He began west again, his back set against the sunrise, heading toward the ocean, realizing that a great passage of his life had come and gone. “I loved you, Jake,” he said aloud.</span></p>
<a aid="H5AL9"></a>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ALA"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ALB">The stiffness wore out of his body and he began to walk more rapidly. By that evening he had come to the end of the land. He sat on a beach which stretched left and right forever, deserted. The waves beat endlessly against the shore, pounding and pounding. The setting sun painted the water in a wide strip of fool’s gold.</span></p>
<p class="calibre_10" aid="H5ALC"><span class="calibre3" aid="H5ALD">There the gunslinger sat, his face turned up into the fading light. He dreamed his dreams and watched as the stars came out; his purpose did not flag, nor did his heart falter; his hair, finer now and gray at the temples, blew around his head, and the sandalwood-inlaid guns of his father lay smooth and deadly against his hips, and he was lonely but did not find loneliness in any way a bad or ignoble thing. The dark came down and the world moved on. The gunslinger waited for the time of the <span class="italic" aid="H5ALE">drawing</span> and dreamed his long dreams of the Dark Tower, to which he would someday come at dusk and approach, winding his horn, to do some unimaginable final battle.</span></p><p class="calibre10" aid="H5ALF"> </p>
<p class="calibre_" aid="H5ALG"><img alt="thegunsling_261_0.jpg" class="calibre13" src="kindle:embed:000J?mime=image/jpeg"/></p>

In later volumes, it somehow became the name of a <span class="italic" aid="K0RQ5">man:</span> the rebel John Farson, who engineers the fall of Gilead, the city-state where Roland spends his childhood.</span></p>  <div class="mbp_pagebreak" id="calibre_pb_39" aid="K0RQ6"></div>
